<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-three-introduction-to-fungi-mycology">Chapter Three: Introduction to Fungi (Mycology)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-three-introduction-to-fungi-mycology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The Study of Fungi is called Mycology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-1-main-characteristics-of-fungi">3.1. Main Characteristics of Fungi:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-1-main-characteristics-of-fungi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Eukaryotic cells</li>
<li>Non-photosynthetic (heterotrophic)</li>
<li>Most fungi are multicellular</li>
<li>Most fungi are microscopic molds or yeasts</li>
<li>Fungal cell wall:</li>
<li>The cell walls of Fungi are made of chitin (polysaccharides)</li>
<li>Some fungi have cross walls, or septa, which divide the filaments into compartments having a single nucleus.</li>
<li>Filaments of fungi are called hyphae.</li>
<li>The mycelium is a mat of hyphae visible to the unaided eye (e.g. bread mold)</li>
<li>Some hyphae may divided by cross sections called septa</li>
<li>Some cells lack septa and are multi-nucleated, or coenocytic (have many nuclei)</li>
<li>The Primary Structures of a Fungi:</li>
<li>Spores (haploid reproductive cell)</li>
<li>Hypha (a single filament)</li>
<li>Mycelium (a mass of hyphae)</li>
<li>Fruiting Body (reproductive and dispersion)</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-8b969542.jpeg" alt="img-34.jpeg">
Structure of Fungi</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-0a824dea.jpeg" alt="img-35.jpeg"></p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-51d1c01b.jpeg" alt="img-36.jpeg">
Structure of Fungi</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-9ee9bd63.jpeg" alt="img-37.jpeg">
The Mycelium growth in a Petri Dish</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-2-fungi-reproduction">3.2. Fungi Reproduction:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-2-fungi-reproduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Fungi reproduce both sexually and asexually.</li>
<li>Asexual reproduction includes:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>fragmentation: the breaking up of hypha</li>
<li>budding: the pinching off of a small hypha outgrowth</li>
<li>asexual spores: theres two kinds of asexual spores</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on
35
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Sporangiospores are produced by sporangia which are located on top of a filament called a sporangiophore.</li>
<li>Conidia are formed at the tips of specialized hyphae called conidiophores.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-420f621f.jpeg" alt="img-38.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-a2afacf9.jpeg" alt="img-39.jpeg"></p>
<p>The Conidiophores look like tubes... the conidia look like small black dots inside the tubes</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-3-classification-of-fungi">3.3. Classification of Fungi:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-3-classification-of-fungi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fungi are mostly classified by the shape of the reproductive structures (Fruiting Bodies)</p>
<ul>
<li>Phylum Zygomycota (e.g. bread mold)</li>
<li>Phylum Basidiomycota (e.g. mushrooms, puff balls, bracket fungi)</li>
<li>Phylum Ascomycota (cup fungi)</li>
<li>Phylum Deuteromycota (Imperfect fungi)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-phylum-zygomycota">1. Phylum Zygomycota:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-phylum-zygomycota" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A common Zygomycota is Bread Mold</li>
<li>Hyphae lack septa</li>
<li>Sexual reproduction is by conjugation (fusing) hyphae from two different strains, followed by plasmogamy, karyogamy and meiosis and the production of Zygospores.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-261aaf79.jpeg" alt="img-40.jpeg">
Asexual reproduction in Zygomycota</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-4ff6317c.jpeg" alt="img-41.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-phylum-basidiomycota">2. Phylum Basidiomycota:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-phylum-basidiomycota" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Mushrooms, Puffballs, or Shelf (Bracket) Fungi</li>
<li>Have Septa and reproduce sexually</li>
<li>Underground hyphae intertwine and grow upward to produce a reproductive structure called a basidiocarp. This basidiocarp is what we call a mushroom.</li>
<li>Basidiospores are produced on the basidia, reproductive structures, which are found on the edges of the gills.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-12d8c3f0.jpeg" alt="img-42.jpeg">
Agaricus</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-e3ebf0f1.jpeg" alt="img-43.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-phylum-ascomycota">3. Phylum Ascomycota:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-phylum-ascomycota" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The largest group of fungi</p>
<ul>
<li>Named for the reproductive sacs or Asci that form near the tips of the hyphae.</li>
<li>Ascospores are formed here and released into the air when the ascus ruptures. These spores germinate to form new hyphae.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>

Cup Fungi</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-phylum-deuteromycota">4. Phylum Deuteromycota:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-phylum-deuteromycota" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Athletes Foot</li>
<li>The Deuteromycetes (Imperfect Fungi)</li>
<li>Fungi for which a sexual stage has not been observed.</li>
<li>All reproduce by conidia</li>
<li>Called imperfect because a sexual reproductive stage has not been observed.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-bff51ed3.jpeg" alt="img-45.jpeg">
Athletes Foot caused by Epidermophyton floccosum</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-66a18be3.jpeg" alt="img-46.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-4-mode-of-life-of-fungi">3.4. Mode of life of fungi<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-4-mode-of-life-of-fungi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-saprophyte">1. Saprophyte:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-saprophyte" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Most fungi are saprophytes, which break down dead matter and play a vital role in the recycling of nutrients.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Extracellular Digestion  this is what is going on our own stomachs except it is done outside of the body of the fungi. The resulting nutrients (smaller molecules of the original organic matter) are brought into the fungi through diffusion. The nutrients are then used for growth and repair.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-parasitic-fungi">2. Parasitic Fungi:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-parasitic-fungi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These fungi can cause diseases in plants and animals.</li>
<li>Examples: athlete's foot and ringworm (Tinea)</li>
<li>These fungi feed on living cells. They have special hyphae (haustoria), that drink from the host cell without killing it immediately.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-21db9663.jpeg" alt="img-47.jpeg">
Plant and animal disease caused by fungi</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-9cf074f9.jpeg" alt="img-48.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-symbiotic-fungi">3. Symbiotic Fungi:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-symbiotic-fungi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Symbiosis is an interaction between two organisms living together in more or less intimate association or even the merging of two dissimilar organisms that bond and interact as a living element.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mycorrhizas">Mycorrhizas:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mycorrhizas" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Mutualism between Fungus (nutrient &amp; water uptake for plant) and Plant (carbohydrate for fungus)</li>
<li>Several kinds:</li>
<li>Zygomycota  hyphae invade root cells</li>
<li>Ascomycota &amp; Basidiomycota  hyphae invade root but dont penetrate cells</li>
</ul>

studocu

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lichens">Lichens<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lichens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>"Mutualism" between Fungus  structure and Alga or cyanobacterium  provides food</li>
</ul>
<p>Form a thallus</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-f1050e0d.jpeg" alt="img-50.jpeg"></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-5-human-and-ecological-relevance-of-fungi">3.5. Human and Ecological Relevance of fungi<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-5-human-and-ecological-relevance-of-fungi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Penicillium Molds:</li>
</ul>
<p>Antibiotics production (Penicillin) &amp; Gourmet Cheese</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Aspergillus:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Production of Citric Acid and Soy Sauce,</p>
</li>

</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-four-introduction-to-algae-phycology">Chapter Four: Introduction to Algae (Phycology)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-four-introduction-to-algae-phycology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-1-characteristics-of-algae">4.1. Characteristics of algae<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-1-characteristics-of-algae" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Algae have a widespread occurrence:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Aquatic habitat: marine, freshwater</li>
<li>Terrestrial habitat: deserts, soils, trees, rocks, etc</li>
<li>Some are symbiotic</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>e.g. lichen is a symbiotic alliance between a fungus and an alga.</li>
<li>e.g. Green Algae (zooxanthellae) live within reef building corals.</li>
<li>Plant-like seaweeds</li>
<li>Lack true leaves, stems &amp; roots</li>
<li>May be filamentous, grow in mats or crusts, sheets, or kelp</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="growth-forms-of-algae">Growth forms of algae:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#growth-forms-of-algae" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Algae take on a variety of forms both microscopic and macroscopic</li>
<li>Unicellular; Colonies; Filaments; Multicellular thallus</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-30935797.jpeg" alt="img-52.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-4919bf81.jpeg" alt="img-53.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-4a1b590d.jpeg" alt="img-54.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-2-major-groups-of-algae">4.2. Major groups of algae:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-2-major-groups-of-algae" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Diatoms: Bacillariophyta</li>
<li>Red algae: Rhodophyceae</li>
<li>Brown algae: Phaeophyceae</li>
<li>Green algae: Chlorophyta</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-division-bacillariophyta-diatoms">1. Division: <em>Bacillariophyta</em> (Diatoms)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-division-bacillariophyta-diatoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Large group of algae (many unidentified). Relatively recently evolved group</li>
<li>Habitat: Diatoms live in cool oceans</li>
<li>Structure: mostly unicellular, have silica in their cell walls</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-a607c5f7.jpeg" alt="img-55.jpeg">
Diatoms</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-division-phaeophyta-brown-algae">2. Division: <em>Phaeophyta</em> (brown algae)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-division-phaeophyta-brown-algae" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Brown/yellow pigment: <em>Fucxanthin</em> and <em>chlorophyll</em> a &amp; c</li>
<li>Diverse morphologies: Simple to large &amp; complex up to 100 m</li>
<li>Fast growing kelp 1 to 2 feet a day</li>
<li>Important source of alginate: Thickener, stabilizer, emulsifier in many products</li>
<li>Body form: Thallus (plant-like but lacks true roots, stems and leaves)</li>
<li>Thallus includes holdfast, stipe and leaflike blades</li>
<li>Cell walls contain cellulose.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-7ff37a17.jpeg" alt="img-56.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-2efdf4e3.jpeg" alt="img-57.jpeg"></p>
<p>42</p>
<p>43</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-division-rhodophyta-red-algae">3. Division: Rhodophyta (Red algae)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-division-rhodophyta-red-algae" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Red pigments: Phycobilins and Chlorophyll a</li>
<li>Coralline algae</li>
<li>Cell walls: cellulose, some with CaCO</li>
<li>CaCO in cell walls: Defense and structure</li>
<li>Source of carrageenan &amp; agar (emulsifiers &amp; gel thickeners)</li>
<li>~5,500 species, mostly marine and few freshwater</li>
<li>Live attached to surfaces (rocks, shells, other algae)</li>
<li>Many are reef-building algae</li>
<li>Body forms: Unicellular, simple filaments or complex filamentous aggregations</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-2d5f9ec0.jpeg" alt="img-58.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-7996fee4.jpeg" alt="img-59.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-division-chlorophyta-green-algae">4. Division: Chlorophyta (Green algae)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-division-chlorophyta-green-algae" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Green pigments: Chlorophyll a &amp; b</li>
<li>Diverse morphologies: Filamentous &amp; Sheets &amp; Spongy and Calcareous (Important component of coral reef environments)</li>
<li>Fossil record: 1.5-2 BYA</li>
<li>~8,000 species (500 genera)</li>
<li>Marine, freshwater, terrestrial.</li>
<li>Attached or planktonic.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Many species form symbiotic relationships with other organisms.</li>
<li>Unicellular, filaments, colonies, also thallus body form.</li>
<li>Cell walls: absent, cellulose, or modifications</li>
<li>Many taxonomists believe green algae (and red algae) should be included among the Plantae.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-d24e6014.jpeg" alt="img-60.jpeg">
Green algae</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-3-ecological-importance-of-algae">4.3. Ecological Importance of algae:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-3-ecological-importance-of-algae" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Are very important primary producers especially in marine ecosystems</li>
<li>Play major roles in global cycling of C, N, and O.</li>
<li>Their photosynthetic activity forms the basis of complex communities.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-five-introduction-to-protozoa-protozoology">Chapter Five: Introduction to Protozoa (Protozoology)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-five-introduction-to-protozoa-protozoology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-1-characteristics-of-protozoa">5.1. Characteristics of Protozoa:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-1-characteristics-of-protozoa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Unicellular Organization: Since Protozoa are single celled they often rely on other organisms for some necessities</li>
<li>Reproduction:</li>
<li>Asexual:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Binary fission: cytoplasmic division follows mitosis, producing two organisms</li>
<li>Budding:</li>
<li>Multiple fission or schizogeny: cell or organism is split into many new cells or organisms</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Sexual</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-90ab1164.jpeg" alt="img-61.jpeg">
Reproduction in Protozoa</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symbiosis">Symbiosis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symbiosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An intimate association between two organisms and there are three types of symbiosis:</p>
<ol>
<li>Parasitism: one organism lives in or on a second organism, called the host. The host is harmed, but usually survives</li>
<li>Commensalism: one organism benefits and the other neither benefits nor is harmed</li>
<li>Mutualism: both organisms benefit from the relationship</li>
</ol>

Protozoan Taxonomy:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-2-protozoan-taxonomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-phylum-sarcomastigophora">1. Phylum Sarcomastigophora<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-phylum-sarcomastigophora" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics">Characteristics:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>18,000 species, largest protozoan phylum</li>
<li>Unicellular or Colonial</li>
<li>Locomotion by flagella, pseudopodia, or both</li>
<li>Autotrophic, saprozoic, or heterotrophic</li>
<li>Single type of Nucleus</li>
<li>Sexual Reproduction (usually)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="subphylum-mastigophora">Subphylum Mastigophora:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#subphylum-mastigophora" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Locomotion is by one or more flagella</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-84e1ab1e.jpeg" alt="img-62.jpeg"></p>
<p>Subphylum Mastigophora</p>
<p>47</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="subphylum-sarcodina">Subphylum Sarcodina:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#subphylum-sarcodina" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Locomotion and food gathered by <em>pseudopodia</em> (false foot)</li>
<li><em>Pseudopodia</em> is temporary cell extension used for movement and gathering food</li>
<li>includes the Amoeba</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-3b8ecde9.jpeg" alt="img-63.jpeg">
Amoeba</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-phylum-apicomplexa">2. Phylum Apicomplexa:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-phylum-apicomplexa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="characteristics">Characteristics:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>All are parasites</li>
<li>Apical complex for penetrating host cells</li>
<li>Single type of Nucleus</li>
<li>Usually <em>No Cilia</em> and <em>Flagella</em></li>
<li>Life cycles that typically include asexual and sexual phases</li>
</ul>

<p>Malaria caused by Plasmodium</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-phylum-ciliophora">3. Phylum Ciliophora<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-phylum-ciliophora" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="characteristics">Characteristics:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Cilia for locomotion and for the generation of feeding currents of water. Cilia are generally similar to flagella but are much shorter, more numerous and widely distributed over the surface of the organism</li>
<li>Relatively rigid pellicle and more or less fixed shape</li>
<li>Distinct cytostome (mouth) Structure</li>
<li>Dimorphic nuclei, typically larger macronuclei and one more smaller micronuclei</li>
<li>Some ciliates possess an oral groove</li>
<li>cilia sweep food particles down this groove toward the cytopharynx where a food vacuole forms</li>
<li>Some ciliates even possess an anal pore which is used to remove waste from the organism</li>
<li>Ciliate have two kinds of nuclei</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Macronuclei: large polyploid nucleus that regulates daily metabolic activities</li>
<li>Micronuclei: one or more small nucleus which are genetic reserve of the cell</li>
</ul>
<ol start="9">
<li>Ciliates can reproduce asexually by transverse binary fission and occasionally by budding</li>
<li>Ciliates can reproduce sexually by conjugation</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-bbfa82c7.jpeg" alt="img-65.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="conjugation">Conjugation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conjugation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Random contact brings individuals of opposite mating types together (called conjugants)</li>
<li>Meiosis results in four haploid pronuclei</li>
<li>Three pronuclei and the macronucleus degenerate. Mitosis and mutual exchange of pronuclei is followed by fusion of the pronuclei.</li>
<li>Conjugants separate. Nuclear divisions that restore nuclear characteristics of species follow. Cytoplasmic divisions may accompany these events.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-fc2340ed.jpeg" alt="img-66.jpeg">
Conjugation</p>

<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-six-introduction-to-virus-virology">Chapter Six: Introduction to Virus (Virology)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-six-introduction-to-virus-virology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-1-viral-characteristics">6.1. Viral Characteristics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-1-viral-characteristics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Virus" is from the Greek meaning for "poison" and was initially described by Edward Jenner in 1798</li>
<li>Virus is a package of genetic information protected by a protein shell for delivery into a host cell to be expressed and replicated</li>
<li>Nucleic acid (DNA or RNA)</li>
<li>Lack of nuclear membrane and external cell wall</li>
<li>They have very small genomes, produce limited numbers of proteins and do not possess many intracellular systems ie they are parasites &gt; intracellular replication</li>
<li>Viruses  three basic forms:</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-complex">1. Complex:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-complex" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Poxviruses: No capsid DNA surrounded by core membrane</li>
<li>Bacteriophages: Complex capsid head and tail structures</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-naked-or-non-enveloped">2. Naked or non-enveloped:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-naked-or-non-enveloped" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Capsid which contains DNA or RNA</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-enveloped">3. Enveloped<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-enveloped" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Outer membrane</li>
<li>Capsid which contains DNA or RNA</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="viral-structure">Viral structure:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#viral-structure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Capsomeres are structural subunits containing several proteins</li>
<li>Capsomeres aggregate to produce the viral capsid.</li>
<li>The viral capsid associates with the viral nucleic acid to produce a nucleocapsid</li>
<li>Nucleocapsids are usually arranged in one of three ways</li>
<li>Lipid envelopes are derived from cellular membranes</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Viruses are known to infect every cell type</li>
<li>Obligate intracellular parasites</li>
<li>Namometers in size (20 - 200 nm)</li>
<li>Acellular</li>
<li>No metabolic enzymes</li>
<li>No machinery for protein production</li>
<li>Have instructions for their own reproduction, but not outside of host cell</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-a27e614f.jpeg" alt="img-67.jpeg">
Viral structure:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-2-viral-taxonomy">6.2. Viral taxonomy:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-viral-taxonomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Viral classification is based upon:</p>
<ul>
<li>Shape</li>
<li>Type and form of nucleic acid</li>
<li>Enveloped or naked</li>
<li>Mode of replication</li>
<li>Organization of the genome and antigenic differences</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-are-viruses-classified">How are viruses classified?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-are-viruses-classified" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hierarchical virus classification: Order- Family - subfamily - genus - species - strain/type</li>
<li>All families have the suffix viridae, e.g Herpesviridae</li>
<li>Genera have the suffix virus. For instance Coxsackie virus</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-fb9a0692.jpeg" alt="img-68.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-3-genomic-organization-of-viral-nucleic-acids">6.3. Genomic organization of viral nucleic acids:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-3-genomic-organization-of-viral-nucleic-acids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-rna-viruses">1. RNA viruses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-rna-viruses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>RNA single stranded: positive polarity or negative polarity</li>
<li>RNA double stranded: one piece or segmented</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-dna-viruses">2. DNA viruses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-dna-viruses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Single stranded</li>
<li>Double stranded</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-f6ca5380.jpeg" alt="img-69.jpeg"></p>
<p>6.4. Viral Host Range:</p>
<ol>
<li>Tropisms: viral tissue specificities</li>
<li>Restricted: Human liver cells  hepatitis B</li>
<li>Intermediate: Intestinal and nerve cells of primates - poliovirus</li>
<li>Broad: Various cells of all mammals  rabies</li>
</ol>
<p>How do you acquire these viral infections?</p>
<ul>
<li>Direct personal contact: Herpes viruses, HIV, Influenza</li>
<li>Airborne spread: Chicken pox</li>
<li>Parenteral: HIV, Hepatitis B and C, cytomegalovirus (CMV)</li>
<li>Fomites: Enteroviruses and other sturdy drying resistant viruses</li>
<li>Vectors: West Nile</li>
<li>Vertical transmission: HIV, Herpes simplex, cytomegalovirus, rubella (German measles)</li>
<li>Enteral (foodborne): Hepatitis A, gastroenteritis viruses</li>
</ul>
<p>6.5. Viral Life Cycles:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Adsorption/Docking:
Specific interactions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Penetration:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Receptor mediated endocytosis</li>
<li>Vesicle fuses with lysosome</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Uncoating: Enzymes in lysosome digest capsid, envelope (if present) and release viral genome</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Replication:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Copies of viral genome</li>
<li>Copies of viral proteins</li>
</ul>

Release:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-release" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-seven-introduction-to-microbial-metabolism">Chapter Seven: Introduction to Microbial Metabolism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-seven-introduction-to-microbial-metabolism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-1-metabolism">7.1. Metabolism:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-1-metabolism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The sum of the chemical reactions in an organism</li>
<li>A metabolic pathway is a sequence of enzymatically catalyzed chemical reactions in a cell.</li>
<li>Metabolic pathways are determined by enzymes.</li>
<li>Enzymes are encoded by genes.</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>
<p><strong>Catabolism</strong>: The energy-releasing processes. Catabolism provides the building blocks and energy for anabolism</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Anabolism</strong>: The energy-using processes</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-44e8f2bc.jpeg" alt="img-72.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>The collision theory states that chemical reactions can occur when atoms, ions, and molecules collide.</li>
<li>Activation energy is needed to disrupt electronic configurations.</li>
<li>Reaction rate is the frequency of collisions with enough energy to bring about a reaction.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Reaction rate can be increased by enzymes or by increasing temperature or pressure.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-0185ab9b.jpeg" alt="img-73.jpeg">
Enzyme</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-2-enzymes">7.2. Enzymes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-2-enzymes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Biological catalysts</li>
<li>Specific for a chemical reaction; not used up in that reaction</li>
<li>Apoenzyme: Protein</li>
<li>Cofactor: Nonprotein component</li>
</ul>
<p>Coenzyme: Organic cofactor (NAD, NADP, FAD, Coenzyme A)</p>
<ul>
<li>Holoenzyme: Apoenzyme plus cofactor</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-08130e48.jpeg" alt="img-74.jpeg">
Key-Lock theory of enzyme activity</p>

5studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="enzyme-classification">Enzyme Classification:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#enzyme-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Oxidoreductase: Oxidation-reduction reactions</li>
<li>Transferase: Transfer functional groups</li>
<li>Hydrolase: Hydrolysis</li>
<li>Lyase: Removal of atoms without hydrolysis</li>
<li>Isomerase: Rearrangement of atoms</li>
<li>Ligase: Joining of molecules, uses ATP</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-influencing-enzyme-activity">Factors Influencing Enzyme Activity:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-influencing-enzyme-activity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Enzymes can be denatured by temperature and pH</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-dcae542b.jpeg" alt="img-75.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-6e31dc9b.jpeg" alt="img-76.jpeg">
Factors Influencing Enzyme Activity</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-45fb54e4.jpeg" alt="img-77.jpeg"></p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="oxidation-reduction-reaction">Oxidation-Reduction Reaction:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#oxidation-reduction-reaction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Oxidation is the removal of electrons.</li>
<li>Reduction is the gain of electrons.</li>
<li>Redox reaction is an oxidation reaction paired with a reduction reaction.</li>
<li>In biological systems, the electrons are often associated with hydrogen atoms. Biological oxidations are often dehydrogenations</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-e5cd79b3.jpeg" alt="img-78.jpeg"></p>
<p>Oxidation-Reduction Reaction:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-3-carbohydrate-catabolism">7.3. Carbohydrate Catabolism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-3-carbohydrate-catabolism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The breakdown of carbohydrates to release energy which are carried out through three major processes:</p>
<ol>
<li>Glycolysis</li>
<li>Krebs cycle</li>
<li>Electron transport chain</li>
</ol>
<p>58</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-glycolysis">1. Glycolysis:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-glycolysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The oxidation of glucose to pyruvic acid produces ATP and NADH.</p>
<p>Glucose + 2 ATP + 2 ADP + 2 PO + 2 NAD  2 pyruvic acid + 4 ATP + 2 NADH + 2H</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-5c0f7f9d.jpeg" alt="img-79.jpeg"></p>
<p>Glycolysis cycle</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-krebs-cycle-citric-acid-cycle">2. Krebs Cycle (Citric acid cycle):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-krebs-cycle-citric-acid-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Oxidation of acetyl CoA produces NADH and FADH</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-d8fac716.jpeg" alt="img-80.jpeg">
Krebs Cycle (Citric acid cycle):</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-electron-transport-chain">3. Electron transport chain:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-electron-transport-chain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Oxidation of molecules liberates electrons for an electron transport chain.</li>
<li>ATP is generated by oxidative phosphorylation</li>
<li>Aerobic respiration: The final electron acceptor in the electron transport chain is molecular oxygen (O)</li>
<li>Anaerobic respiration: The final electron acceptor in the electron transport chain is not O and it yields less energy than aerobic respiration because only part of the Krebs cycles operations under anaerobic conditions</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-dac97111.jpeg" alt="img-81.jpeg">
Electron transport chain</p>
<p>ATP produced from complete oxidation of one glucose using aerobic respiration:</p>
<p>36 ATPs are produced.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Pathway</th><th>By substrate-level phosphorylation</th><th>By oxidative phosphorylation</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td></td><td></td><td>From NADH</td><td>From FADH</td></tr><tr><td>Glycolysis</td><td>2</td><td>6</td><td>0</td></tr><tr><td>Intermediate step</td><td>0</td><td>6</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Krebs cycle</td><td>2</td><td>18</td><td>4</td></tr><tr><td>Total</td><td>4</td><td>30</td><td>4</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fermentation">Fermentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fermentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Releases energy from oxidation of organic molecules</li>
<li>Does not require oxygen</li>
<li>Does not use the Krebs cycle or Electron transport chain (ETC)</li>
<li>Uses an organic molecule as the final electron acceptor
Alcohol fermentation: Produces ethyl alcohol + CO2.
Lactic acid fermentation: Produces lactic acid.</li>
<li>Homolactic fermentation: Produces lactic acid only.</li>
<li>Heterolactic fermentation: Produces lactic acid and other compounds.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-5-photosynthesis">7.5. Photosynthesis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-5-photosynthesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Photo: Conversion of light energy into chemical energy (ATP)</li>
<li>Light-dependent (light) reactions</li>
<li>Synthesis: Fixing carbon into organic molecules</li>
<li>Light-independent (dark) reaction, Calvin-Benson cycle</li>
<li>Oxygen:</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-6-nutritional-categories-of-microorganisms">7.6. Nutritional Categories of Microorganisms:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-6-nutritional-categories-of-microorganisms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Microorganisms are often grouped according to the sources of energy they use:</p>
<ol>
<li>Phototrophs use light as an energy source (Photosynthesis)</li>
<li>Chemotrophs use chemicals as energy sources</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Chemoorganotroph</li>
<li>Chemolithotroph</li>
</ul>
<p>Metabolic Diversity among Organisms:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Nutritional type</th><th>Energy source</th><th>Carbon source</th><th>Example</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Photoautotroph</td><td>Light</td><td>CO_{2}</td><td>Oxygenic: Cyanobacteria plants. Anoxygenic: Green, purple bacteria.</td></tr><tr><td>Photoheterotroph</td><td>Light</td><td>Organic compounds</td><td>Green, purple nonsulfur bacteria.</td></tr><tr><td>Chemoautotroph</td><td>Chemical</td><td>CO</td><td>Iron-oxidizing bacteria.</td></tr><tr><td>Chemoheterotroph</td><td>Chemical</td><td>Organic compounds</td><td>Fermentative bacteria. Animals, protozoa, fungi, bacteria.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>64</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-eight-introduction-to-microbial-genetics">Chapter Eight: Introduction to Microbial Genetics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-eight-introduction-to-microbial-genetics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Genetics: The study of what genes are, how they carry information, how information is expressed, and how genes are replicated.</li>
<li>Gene: A segment of DNA that encodes a functional product, usually a protein.</li>
<li>Genome: All of the genetic material in a cell</li>
<li>Genomics: The molecular study of genomes</li>
<li>Genotype: The genes of an organism</li>
<li>Phenotype: Expression of the genes</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-93c2641f.jpeg" alt="img-86.jpeg">
Flow of Genetic Information</p>

<p>DNA/Base sequences</p>

Chromosome Map</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="deoxyribonucleic-acid-dna">Deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#deoxyribonucleic-acid-dna" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Polymer of nucleotides: Adenine, thymine, cytosine, and guanine</li>
<li>Double helix associated with proteins</li>
<li>"Backbone" is deoxyribose-phosphate</li>
<li>Strands are held together by hydrogen bonds between AT and CG.</li>
<li>Strands are antiparallel.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-dcc49fbb.jpeg" alt="img-89.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-344afd78.jpeg" alt="img-90.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>DNA is copied by DNA polymerase in the 5'-3' direction</li>
<li>Initiated by an RNA primer</li>
<li>Leading strand is synthesized continuously</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Lagging strand is synthesized discontinuously forming Okazaki fragments</li>
<li>RNA primers are removed and Okazaki fragments joined by a DNA polymerase and DNA ligase</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dna-replication">DNA Replication:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dna-replication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>DNA replication is semiconservative.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-6dca53b1.jpeg" alt="img-91.jpeg"></p>
<p>DNA Replication: DNA replication is semiconservative.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="synthesis-of-protein">Synthesis of Protein<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#synthesis-of-protein" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-transcription">1. Transcription:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-transcription" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>DNA is transcribed to make RNA (mRNA, tRNA, and rRNA).
Transcription begins when RNA polymerase binds to the promotor sequence
Transcription proceeds in the  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>5</mn><mo mathvariant="normal" lspace="0em" rspace="0em"></mo></msup><mo></mo><msup><mn>3</mn><mo mathvariant="normal" lspace="0em" rspace="0em"></mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">5^{\prime}\rightarrow 3^{\prime}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7519em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">5</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.7519em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7519em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">3</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.7519em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  direction
Transcription stops when it reaches the terminator sequence</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-translation">2. Translation:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-translation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>mRNA is translated in codons (three nucleotides)</li>
<li>Translation of mRNA begins at the start codon: AUG</li>
<li>Translation ends at a stop codon: UAA, UAG, UGA</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mutation">Mutation:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mutation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A change in the genetic material</li>
<li>Mutations may be neutral, beneficial, or harmful.</li>
<li>Mutagen: Agent that causes mutations</li>
<li>Spontaneous mutations: Occur in the absence of a mutagen</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-base-substitution-point-mutation">1. Base substitution (point mutation):<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-base-substitution-point-mutation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Missense mutation</li>
<li>Change in one base resulting in change in amino acid</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-d469d634.jpeg" alt="img-96.jpeg">
<img src="assets/images/image-20260115-a99ac0b0.jpeg" alt="img-97.jpeg">

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-frameshift-mutation">3. Frameshift mutation:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-frameshift-mutation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Insertion or deletion of one or more nucleotide pairs</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-57eb48b5.jpeg" alt="img-100.jpeg">
<img src="assets/images/image-20260115-31dae618.jpeg" alt="img-101.jpeg">
Frameshift mutation</p>
