<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-mutations">Causes of mutations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-mutations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Spontaneous mutations</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Occur in the absence of mutation causing agents</li>
<li>Due to occasional mistakes in DNA replication</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Induced mutations:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Caused by mutagens, agents such as chemicals and radiation which induce mutations</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chemical mutagens:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nitrous acid alters adenine such that it pairs with cytosine instead of thymine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ethidium bromide inserts between bases causing frameshift mutation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Radiation:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Ionizing radiation (X-rays and gamma rays)
Causes the formation of ions that can react with nucleotides (causing base changes) and the deoxyribose-phosphate backbone (causes chromosomes to break).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>UV radiation
Induces formation of covalent bonds between adjacent thymines to form thymine dimers which can not be replicate</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-11ed0b19.jpeg" alt="img-102.jpeg"></p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-nine-introduction-into-environmental-microbiology">Chapter Nine: Introduction into Environmental Microbiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-nine-introduction-into-environmental-microbiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Environmental Microbiology: Studies the microorganisms as they occur in their natural habitats</li>
<li>Microbes flourish in every habitat on Earth</li>
<li>Microbes are important to the cycling of chemical elements</li>
<li>Microbial Ecology: Study of the interrelationships among microorganisms and the environment</li>
<li>Two aspects to consider:</li>
<li>Levels of microbial associations in the environment</li>
<li>Role of adaptation in microbial survival</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="microbial-ecology">Microbial Ecology:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#microbial-ecology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Role of adaptation in microbial survival</li>
<li>Most microorganisms live in harsh environments</li>
<li>Microbes must be specially adapted to survive</li>
<li>Microbes must adapt to constantly varying conditions</li>
<li>Extremophiles: Adapted to extremely harsh conditions</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="biodiversity-held-in-balance-by-various-checks">Biodiversity held in balance by various checks:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#biodiversity-held-in-balance-by-various-checks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Competition</li>
<li>Antagonism</li>
<li>Cooperation</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-1-soil-microbiology">9.1. Soil Microbiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-1-soil-microbiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Examines the roles played by organisms living in soil</li>
<li>Nature of soils</li>
<li>Soil arises from the weathering of rocks</li>
<li>Soil also produced through the actions of microorganisms</li>
</ul>

studocu

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="environmental-factors-affecting-microbial-abundance-in-soils">Environmental factors affecting microbial abundance in soils:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environmental-factors-affecting-microbial-abundance-in-soils" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Moisture content: Moist soils support microbial growth better than dry soils</li>
<li>Oxygen: Moist soils are lower in oxygen than dry soils (Oxygen dissolves poorly in water)</li>
<li>pH: Highly acidic and highly basic soils favor fungi</li>
<li>Temperature: Most soil organisms are mesophiles</li>
<li>Nutrient availability: Microbial community size determined by how much organic material is available</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-c3b3c470.jpeg" alt="img-103.jpeg"></p>
<p>The soil layers and the distributions of nutrients and microorganisms within them</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="microbial-populations-present-in-the-soil-include">Microbial populations present in the soil include:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#microbial-populations-present-in-the-soil-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Bacteria</li>
<li>Archaea</li>
<li>Fungi</li>
<li>Algae and protozoa</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="microbes-perform-a-number-of-functions">Microbes perform a number of functions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#microbes-perform-a-number-of-functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cycle elements and convert them to usable form</li>
<li>Degrade dead organisms</li>
<li>Produce compounds with potential human uses</li>
</ul>

<p>73</p>
<p>Table 1: Selected Soilborne Diseases of Humans and Plants</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Selected Soilborne Diseases of Humans and Plants</th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Microorganism</td><td>Host</td><td>Disease</td></tr><tr><td>Bacteria</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Bacillus anthracis</td><td>Humans</td><td>Anthrax</td></tr><tr><td>Clostridium tetani</td><td>Humans</td><td>Tetanus</td></tr><tr><td>Agrobacterium tumefaciens</td><td>Plants</td><td>Crown gall disease</td></tr><tr><td>Ralstonia solanacearum</td><td>Plants</td><td>Potato wilt</td></tr><tr><td>Streptomyces scabies</td><td>Plants</td><td>Potato scab</td></tr><tr><td>Fungi</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Histoplasma capsulatum</td><td>Humans</td><td>Histoplasmosis</td></tr><tr><td>Blastomyces dermatitidis</td><td>Humans</td><td>Blastomycosis</td></tr><tr><td>Coccidioides immitis</td><td>Humans</td><td>Coccidioidomycosis</td></tr><tr><td>Polymyxa spp.</td><td>Plants</td><td>Root rot in cereals</td></tr><tr><td>Fusarium oxysporum</td><td>Plants</td><td>Root rot in many plants</td></tr><tr><td>Phytophthora cinnamomi</td><td>Plants</td><td>Potato blight; root rot in many plants</td></tr><tr><td>Viruses</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Hantavirus</td><td>Humans</td><td>Hantavirus pulmonary syndrome</td></tr><tr><td>Tobacco mosaic virus</td><td>Plants</td><td>Necrotic spots in various plants</td></tr><tr><td>Soilborne wheat mosaic virus</td><td>Plants</td><td>Mosaic disease in winter wheat and barley</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Rhizosphere:</p>
<p>Soil in direct contact with plant root is enriched in nutrients as a result of nearby plant activities</p>
<p>Organic material in rhizosphere:</p>
<ol>
<li>Exudates: low molecular weight compounds released from plant cells in a non-metabolic manner (leakage)</li>
<li>Secretions: compounds metabolically released from plant cells</li>
<li>Lysates: compounds released from moribund cells during autolysis</li>
<li>Plant mucilage: plant polysaccharides</li>
</ol>

<ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="9-2-aquatic-microbiology">9.2. Aquatic Microbiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-2-aquatic-microbiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Aquatic Microbiology: Study of microbes living in freshwater and marine environments</li>
<li>Ecology of aquatic environments is complex</li>
<li>Most aquatic environments are teaming with life</li>
<li>Water ecosystems support fewer microbes than soil due to dilution of nutrients</li>
<li>Marine system constitute about  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>70</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">70\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">70%</span></span></span></span></span>  of the total Earth area</li>
<li>Types of aquatic habitats:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Freshwater systems - characterized by low salt content</li>
<li>Marine systems - characterized by a salt content of  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo></mo><mn>3.5</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\sim 3.5\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">3.5%</span></span></span></span></span></li>
<li>Specialized aquatic systems - salt lakes, iron springs, and sulfur springs</li>
</ol>

<ol>
<li>Drinking Water (Potable): No coliforms contamination acceptable</li>
<li>Recreational water: 200 fecal coliforms /100 ml</li>
<li>Fish and wildlife habitat: 5000 fecal coliforms/100 ml</li>
<li>Shellfish: 14 fecal coliforms/100 ml</li>
</ol>

<ul>
<li><strong>General coliforms</strong>  indicate water in contact with plant or animal life (universally present)</li>

</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="9-3-air-microbiology-aeromicrobiology">9.3. Air Microbiology (Aeromicrobiology)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-3-air-microbiology-aeromicrobiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Aerobiology is defined as the study of life present in the air.</li>
<li>Aeromicrobiology relates to the study of environmentally relevant microorganisms.</li>
<li>Microorganisms exist within 300-1000 feet of earths surface that have become attached to fragments of dried leaves, straw or dust particles light enough to be blown by wind.</li>
<li>In dry whether the microbial load of air is high while in wet weather the rain washes the microorganisms from the air.</li>
<li>Air is a poor medium for microbial growth  too dry and no nutrients</li>
<li>Spore forming and Gram-positive bacteria are resistant to drying</li>
<li>Dust, water droplets in air carry microbial populations from one place to another</li>
<li>Sneezing, coughing, talking are efficient methods of transferring microbes from one respiratory tract to another</li>
<li>Liquid and dust particles settle in the respiratory tract depending on their velocity and size</li>
<li>Microorganisms colonize specific locations in the respiratory tract</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-cbb8c92b.jpeg" alt="img-115.jpeg"></p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-4-food-microbiology">9.4. Food Microbiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-4-food-microbiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Microorganisms are involved in producing many foods and beverages</li>
<li>Fermentation produces desirable characteristics of various foods</li>
<li>Microbial metabolism has other functions</li>
<li>Acts as a preservative</li>
<li>Destroys many pathogenic microbes and toxins</li>
<li>Can add nutritional value in form of vitamins or other nutrients</li>
<li>Microbes are used in food production</li>
<li>Microbes can help control food spoilage</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-roles-of-microorganisms-in-food-production">The roles of microorganisms in food Production:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-roles-of-microorganisms-in-food-production" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Fermentation: Any desirable change to a food or beverage that occurs as a result of microbial growth</li>
<li>Spoilage is unwanted change to a food due to various reasons</li>
<li>Undesirable metabolic reactions</li>
<li>Growth of pathogens</li>
<li>Presence of unwanted microorganisms in the food</li>
<li>Use starter cultures in commercial food and beverage production</li>
<li>Composed of known microorganisms</li>
<li>Consistently perform specific fermentations</li>
<li>Many common products result from fermentation of vegetables, meats, and dairy products</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="foodborne-illnesses">Foodborne Illnesses:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foodborne-illnesses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Consumption of spoiled foods or foods containing harmful microbes or their products</li>
<li>Two categories of food poisoning</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Food infections: Consumption of living microorganisms</li>
<li>Food intoxications: Consumption of microbial toxins rather than the microbe</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms include nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, fever, fatigue, and muscle cramps</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-ten-introduction-to-industrial-microbiology">Chapter Ten: Introduction to Industrial Microbiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-ten-introduction-to-industrial-microbiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Important field within the microbiological sciences</li>
<li>Industrial microbiology used in various applications</li>
<li>Microbes in fermentation</li>
<li>Microbes in the production of several industrial products</li>
<li>Treatment of water and wastewaters</li>
<li>Disposal and cleanup of biological wastes</li>
<li>Treatment of mine drainage</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-roles-of-microbes-in-industrial-fermentations">The Roles of Microbes in Industrial Fermentations:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-roles-of-microbes-in-industrial-fermentations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Industrial fermentations</li>
<li>Large-scale growth of particular microbes for producing beneficial compounds</li>
<li>Examples include amino acids and vitamins</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-primary-metabolites">1. Primary metabolites<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-primary-metabolites" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Produced during active growth and metabolism</li>
<li>Required for reproduction or are by-products of metabolism</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-secondary-metabolites">2. Secondary metabolites<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-secondary-metabolites" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Produced after the culture has entered stationary growth</li>
<li>Substances are not immediately needed for growth</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-water-treatment">6. Water Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-water-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Wastewater: Water that leaves homes or businesses after use</li>
<li>Wastewater contains a variety of contaminants</li>
<li>Treatment intended to remove or reduce contaminants</li>
<li>Processed to reduce the biochemical oxygen demand (BOD)</li>
<li>Oxygen needed by aerobic bacteria to metabolize wastes</li>
<li>Levels reduced so unable to support microbial growth</li>
</ul>

<p>Chapter Eleven: Introduction to medical microbiology and Immunity</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="11-1-medical-microbiology">11.1. Medical microbiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#11-1-medical-microbiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a6a58dbf">HumanMicrobial Interactions:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a6a58dbf" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Through normal everyday activities, the human body is exposed to <strong>countless microorganisms</strong> in the environment.</li>
<li>In addition, hundreds of species and countless individual microbial cells, collectively referred to as the <strong>normal microbial flora</strong>, grow on or in the <strong>human body</strong>.</li>
<li>Most, but not all, microorganisms are <strong>benign</strong>; a few <strong>contribute</strong> directly to our <strong>health</strong>, and even <strong>fewer</strong> pose direct <strong>threats</strong> to <strong>health</strong>.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="colonization-by-microorganism">Colonization by Microorganism:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#colonization-by-microorganism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Mammals in <strong>utero</strong> develop in a <strong>sterile environment</strong> and have no exposure to microorganisms.</li>
<li>Starting with the <strong>birth process</strong>, colonization, growth of a microorganism after it has gained access to host tissues, begins as animals are <strong>exposed to microorganisms</strong>.</li>
<li>The <strong>skin surfaces</strong> are readily <strong>colonized</strong> by many species.</li>
<li>Likewise, the <strong>oral cavity</strong> and <strong>gastrointestinal tract</strong> acquire microorganisms through feeding and exposure to the mother's body, which, along with other environmental sources, initiates colonization of the skin, oral cavity, upper respiratory tract, and gastrointestinal tract.</li>
<li>Different populations of microorganisms colonize individuals in different localities and at different times.</li>
<li>Genetic factors also play a role. Thus, the <strong>normal microbial flora</strong> is highly dependent on the <strong>conditions</strong> to which an individual is exposed.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The normal flora is highly diverse in each individual and may differ significantly between individuals, even in a given population</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathogen">Pathogen:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathogen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A host is an organism that harbors a parasite, another organism that lives on or in the host and causes damage.</li>
<li>Microbial parasites are called pathogens.</li>
<li>The outcome of a hostparasite relationship depends on pathogenicity, the ability of a parasite to inflict damage on the host.</li>
<li>Pathogenicity differs considerably among potential pathogens, as does the resistance or susceptibility of the host to the pathogen.</li>
<li>An opportunistic pathogen causes disease only in the absence of normal host resistance. Pathogenicity varies markedly for individual pathogens. The quantitative measure of pathogenicity is called virulence.</li>
<li>Neither the virulence of the pathogen nor the relative resistance of the host is a constant factor.</li>
<li>The hostparasite interaction is a dynamic relationship between the two organisms, influenced by changing conditions in the pathogen, the host, and the environment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="infection-and-disease">Infection and Disease:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infection-and-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Infection refers to any situation in which a microorganism is established and growing in a host, whether or not the host is harmed.</li>
<li>Disease is damage or injury to the host that impairs host function.</li>
<li>Infection is not synonymous with disease because growth of a microorganism on a host does not always cause host damage.</li>
<li>Thus, species of the normal microbial flora have infected the host, but seldom cause disease.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>85</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>However, the normal flora sometimes cause disease if <strong>host resistance</strong> is compromised, as happens in diseases such as cancer and acquired immune deficiency syndrome (AIDS).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="f316c364">HostParasite Interactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f316c364" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Animal hosts provide <strong>favorable environments</strong> for the growth of many microorganisms.</li>
<li>They are rich in the organic nutrients and growth factors required by chemoorganotrophs, and provide conditions of controlled pH, osmotic pressure, and temperature.</li>
<li>However, the animal body is <strong>not a uniform</strong> environment.</li>
<li>Each region or <strong>organ</strong> differs <strong>chemically</strong> and <strong>physically</strong> from others and thus provides a selective environment where the growth of certain microorganisms is favored.</li>
<li>For example, the skin, respiratory tract, and gastrointestinal tract provide selective chemical and physical environments that support the growth of a highly diverse microflora.</li>
<li><strong>Animals</strong> also possess <strong>defense mechanisms</strong> that collectively <strong>prevent</strong> or <strong>inhibit</strong> microbial invasion and growth.</li>
<li>The microorganisms that successfully colonize the host have <strong>circumvented</strong> these <strong>defense mechanisms</strong>.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-infection-process">The Infection Process:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-infection-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Infections frequently begin at sites in the animal's <strong>mucous membranes</strong>.</li>
<li><strong>Mucous membranes</strong> consist of single or multiple layers of epithelial cells, tightly packed cells that interface with the external environment.</li>
<li>They are found throughout the body, lining the urogenital, respiratory, and gastrointestinal tracts.</li>
<li>Mucous membranes are frequently coated with a protective layer of viscous soluble glycoproteins called <strong>mucus</strong>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Microorganisms that contact host tissues at mucous membranes may associate loosely with the mucosal surface and are usually swept away by physical processes.</li>
<li>Microorganisms may also adhere more strongly to the epithelial surface as a result of specific cellcell recognition between pathogen and host.</li>
<li>Tissue infection may follow, <strong>breaching</strong> the mucosal barrier and allowing the microorganism to invade deeper into submucosal tissues.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-b2f893bb.jpeg" alt="img-123.jpeg"></p>
<p>Bacterial interactions with mucous membranes. (a) Loose association. (b) Adhesion. (c) Invasion into submucosal epithelial cells.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-0ec96b59.jpeg" alt="img-124.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-ce7bb85e.jpeg" alt="img-125.jpeg"></p>
<p>Microorganisms and mechanisms of pathogenesis</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="11-2-introduction-to-immunology">11.2. Introduction to immunology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#11-2-introduction-to-immunology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Immunity: is a biological term that describes a state of having sufficient biological defenses to avoid infection, disease, or other unwanted biological invasion.</li>
<li>Immunity involves both specific and non-specific components.</li>
<li>The non-specific components act either as barriers or as eliminators of wide range of pathogens irrespective of antigenic specificity.</li>
<li>Other components of the immune system adapt themselves to each new disease encountered and are able to generate pathogen-specific immunity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-innate-immunity">1. Innate immunity:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-innate-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Innate immunity or nonspecific, immunity is the natural resistance with which a person is born.</li>
<li>It provides resistance through several physical, chemical, and cellular approaches.</li>
<li>Microbes first encounter the epithelial layers, physical barriers that line our skin and mucous membranes.</li>
<li>Subsequent general defenses include secreted chemical signals (cytokines), antimicrobial substances, fever, and phagocytic activity associated with the inflammatory response.</li>
<li>The phagocytes express cell surface receptors that can bind and respond to common molecular patterns expressed on the surface of invading microbes. Through these approaches, innate immunity can prevent the colonization, entry, and spread of microbes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-adaptive-immunity">2. Adaptive immunity:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-adaptive-immunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Adaptive immunity is often sub-divided into two major types depending on how the immunity was introduced:
&gt; Naturally acquired immunity occurs through contact with a disease causing agent, when the contact was not deliberate</li>
</ul>
<p>88</p>
<p>&gt; Artificially acquired immunity develops only through deliberate actions such as vaccination.</p>
<ul>
<li>Both naturally and artificially acquired immunity can be further subdivided depending on whether immunity is induced in the host or passively transferred from a immune host.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Passive immunity is acquired through transfer of antibodies or activated T-cells from an immune host, and is short lived  usually lasting only a few months</p>
<p>&gt; Active immunity is induced in the host itself by antigen, and lasts much longer, sometimes life-long. The diagram below summarizes these divisions of immunity.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-40020a86.jpeg" alt="img-126.jpeg"></p>

        // Theme toggle functionality
        const themeToggle = document.getElementById('theme-toggle');
        const html = document.documentElement;
        
        themeToggle.addEventListener('click', () => {
            const currentTheme = html.getAttribute('data-theme');
            const newTheme = currentTheme === 'light' ? 'dark' : 'light';
            
            html.setAttribute('data-theme', newTheme);
            localStorage.setItem('theme', newTheme);
        });
        
        // Load saved theme
        const savedTheme = localStorage.getItem('theme') || 'light';
        html.setAttribute('data-theme', savedTheme);
    </script>

# PDF to HTML Conversion System Prompt (v9.4.4) - Rich UI Edition

**Version:** 9.4.4  
**Last Updated:** December 25, 2025  
**Focus:** Modern UI/UX patterns with 100% content fidelity, nested lists, mathematical equations, and comprehensive interactive quiz system

---

## Overview

This is the comprehensive **PDF to HTML Conversion System Prompt - Rich UI Edition**, featuring enhanced content organization patterns, advanced UI components, mathematical equations support, interactive quiz system, and modern design systems while maintaining absolute content fidelity.

## Core Mission

Convert PDF documents into **visually stunning, accessible, and pedagogically effective** HTML pages while ensuring **100% VERBATIM content preservation**. Create highly appealing and effective learning materials with **modern UI/UX patterns**, that maintain absolute fidelity to the original text content with interactive quizzes to reinforce learning and assess comprehension.

---

##  CRITICAL: ANTI-SUMMARIZATION WARNING

###  ABSOLUTE PROHIBITION ON SUMMARIZATION

**This is the most important rule in this entire prompt:**

> **DO NOT SUMMARIZE, CONDENSE, SHORTEN, OR OMIT ANY CONTENT FROM THE SOURCE TEXT**

Every single paragraph, sentence, list item, heading, table row, callout, and detail from the source text MUST be transferred to the HTML output **verbatim** without exception.

### What This Means in Practice:

|  PROHIBITED |  REQUIRED |
|---------------|-------------|
| Combining multiple paragraphs into one | Keep every paragraph separate |
| Removing "redundant" or similar content | Include all content, even if repetitive |
| Shortening long explanations | Keep full explanations verbatim |
| Omitting examples or illustrations | Include all examples and illustrations |
| Merging list items | Keep every list item separate |
| Skipping introductory/transitional text | Include all introductory and transitional text |
| Simplifying technical language | Keep original wording exactly |
| Removing citations or references | Include all citations and references |
| Condensing tables | Keep complete tables with all rows |
| Excluding "minor" sections | Include ALL sections, regardless of size |

### Mandatory Verification Steps:

1. **Before submitting any HTML file**, run the detection script:
   ```bash
   python3 detect_summarization_simple.py topics/topic-XX.html content_cleaned.txt [start_line] [end_line]
   ```

2. **Acceptable thresholds**:
   - Word count ratio: ** 80%** (above this is acceptable)
   - Paragraph count ratio: ** 90%**
   - List item ratio: ** 85%**
   - H2 heading ratio: ** 90%**

3. **If any indicator shows "LOW" or "MISSING"**, the file is summarizing content and must be fixed.

4. **Common causes of summarization to avoid**:
   - Thinking certain content is "not important"
   - Combining similar paragraphs
   - Removing examples to "save space"
   - Shortening explanations for "brevity"
   - Skipping "obvious" or "well-known" content
   - Merging related concepts into single sections

### Remember:

> **The source text is the authority. If it's in the source, it must be in the HTML. No exceptions.**

---

## Image Handling & Lightbox

All images must be wrapped in a `content-figure` container with the `data-lightbox="true"` attribute to enable the click-to-zoom functionality.

### Image Source Reference

**IMPORTANT**: Use the **exact image filenames** as they appear in `content_cleaned.txt`. Do NOT rename or map images.

#### Image Usage Instructions
1. **Check `content_cleaned.txt`** for image references like:
   ```html
   <img src="assets/images/image-20251225-9d805e34.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg">
   ```
2. **Path Resolution Rule**: Use the correct relative path based on the HTML file's location:
   - **Files in `topics/` directory**: Use `../assets/images/`
   - **Files in root directory** (e.g., `index.html`, `comprehensive-exam.html`): Use `assets/images/`
3. **Do NOT rename** images from their timestamp format
4. **Do NOT use** numbered formats like `img-1.jpeg` - use the actual filename

### HTML Structure for Images

```html
<div class="content-figure" data-lightbox="true">
    <div class="figure-image-wrapper">
        <img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-9d805e34.jpeg" alt="[Alt Text]" class="figure-image">
        <div class="figure-overlay">
            <span class="overlay-icon"></span>
            <span class="overlay-text">Click to zoom</span>
        </div>
    </div>
    <p class="figure-caption">Fig. [X.Y]: [Caption Text]</p>
</div>
```

### Image Path Examples

```html
<!-- Correct: Use exact filenames from content_cleaned.txt -->
<img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-9d805e34.jpeg" alt="Gingivitis showing inflamed gums">
<img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-b2c235cf.jpeg" alt="Fibre-optic Endoscope">
<img src="../assets/images/image-20251225-f38697c2.jpeg" alt="Periodontitis diagram">

<!-- Incorrect: Don't use simplified numbered format -->
<img src="../assets/images/img-1.jpeg" alt="...">
<img src="../assets/images/img-12.jpeg" alt="...">
```

---

## Interactive Quiz System

### Quiz System Overview

The quiz system provides 8 different question types to assess learner comprehension. Quizzes are stored in JSON format with versioning support, rendered dynamically via JavaScript, and fully integrated with the existing Rich UI design system.

### Quiz Question Types

#### 1. Multiple Choice (Single Answer)
Standard single-answer questions with 2-6 options.
- **Use Case**: Testing recall of specific facts, definitions, concepts
- **Features**: Radio button selection, immediate feedback, explanation display

#### 2. Multiple Select (Multiple Correct Answers)
Questions where learners select all correct answers.
- **Use Case**: Testing comprehensive understanding of related concepts
- **Features**: Checkbox selection, partial credit option, "Select all that apply" indicator

#### 3. True/False
Binary choice questions for quick knowledge checks.
- **Use Case**: Verifying understanding of statements, common misconceptions
- **Features**: Two-option format, confidence indicator option

#### 4. Fill in the Blank
Text input questions with exact or fuzzy matching.
- **Use Case**: Testing terminology, formulas, key terms
- **Features**: Case-insensitive matching, multiple acceptable answers, hint system
- **CRITICAL**: Question text MUST include `__id__` placeholders (e.g., `__b1__`, `__b2__`) where input fields should appear
- **Example**: `"The liver converts ammonia into __b1__."` with blank ID `"b1"`

#### 5. Matching
Pair items from two columns (drag-and-drop or dropdown).
- **Use Case**: Testing relationships, associations, categorization
- **Features**: Drag-and-drop interface, dropdown fallback, visual feedback

#### 6. Ordering/Sequencing
Arrange items in correct order.
- **Use Case**: Testing processes, procedures, chronological events
- **Features**: Drag-and-drop reordering with live sorting, numbered positions, step validation
- **Implementation Note**: Use "live" sorting during `dragover` events for robust behavior across all environments (including local `file://` protocol).

#### 7. Short Answer
Free-text response with keyword matching.
- **Use Case**: Testing deeper understanding, explanations
- **Features**: Keyword detection, partial credit, model answer display

#### 8. Image-Based Questions
Questions involving image interaction (hotspots, labeling).
- **Use Case**: Anatomy, diagrams, visual identification
- **Features**: Clickable regions, label placement, image zoom

### Media Support (Optional)

Every question can optionally include media (image, video, audio, YouTube) and answer options can optionally include images. All media fields are **optional** - questions work perfectly with text only.

#### Supported Media Types
| Type | Description | Use Case |
|------|-------------|----------|
| `image` | Static image file | Diagrams, photos, charts |
| `video` | Video file (mp4, webm) | Demonstrations, procedures |
| `audio` | Audio file (mp3, wav) | Pronunciation, sounds |
| `youtube` | YouTube embed | Educational videos |

#### Image Answer Options
For multiple-choice and multiple-select questions, each option can optionally include an image. This is useful for visual identification questions where learners select from images rather than text.

####  CRITICAL: Quiz Media Path Resolution
Image and media paths in quiz data files MUST be relative to the **HTML file** that will host the quiz.
- If the quiz is hosted in a file within `topics/` (e.g., `topics/topic-01.html`), use `../assets/images/`.
- If the quiz is hosted in a file in the **root** (e.g., `comprehensive-exam.html`), use `assets/images/`.

### Quiz JSON Schema (v1.0)

Store quiz data in `quizzes/` directory with the following structure:

```
project-name/
 quizzes/
    quiz-schema.json          # Schema definition
    topic-01-quiz.json        # Quiz for topic 01
    topic-02-quiz.json        # Quiz for topic 02
    ...
```

#### Complete Quiz JSON Schema

```json
{
  "$schema": "http://json-schema.org/draft-07/schema#",
  "title": "Quiz Schema v1.0",
  "type": "object",
  "required": ["schemaVersion", "quizId", "metadata", "questions"],
  "properties": {
    "schemaVersion": {
      "type": "string",
      "description": "Schema version for compatibility",
      "pattern": "^\\d+\\.\\d+$",
      "example": "1.0"
    },
    "quizId": {
      "type": "string",
      "description": "Unique identifier for the quiz",
      "pattern": "^[a-z0-9-]+$"
    },
    "metadata": {
      "type": "object",
      "required": ["title", "topicId", "createdAt"],
      "properties": {
        "title": { "type": "string" },
        "description": { "type": "string" },
        "topicId": { "type": "string" },
        "difficulty": { "enum": ["beginner", "intermediate", "advanced"] },
        "estimatedTime": { "type": "integer", "description": "Minutes" },
        "passingScore": { "type": "integer", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 100 },
        "createdAt": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },
        "updatedAt": { "type": "string", "format": "date-time" },
        "tags": { "type": "array", "items": { "type": "string" } }
      }
    },
    "settings": {
      "type": "object",
      "properties": {
        "shuffleQuestions": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
        "shuffleOptions": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
        "showFeedback": { "enum": ["immediate", "end", "never"], "default": "immediate" },
        "allowRetry": { "type": "boolean", "default": true },
        "showCorrectAnswers": { "type": "boolean", "default": true },
        "timeLimit": { "type": "integer", "description": "Seconds, 0 for unlimited" }
      }
    },
    "questions": {
      "type": "array",
      "items": { "$ref": "#/definitions/question" }
    }
  }
}
```

#### Question Type Definitions

```json
{
  "definitions": {
    "question": {
      "type": "object",
      "required": ["id", "type", "question", "points"],
      "properties": {
        "id": { "type": "string" },
        "type": {
          "enum": [
            "multiple-choice",
            "multiple-select",
            "true-false",
            "fill-blank",
            "matching",
            "ordering",
            "short-answer",
            "image-based"
          ]
        },

        "points": { "type": "integer", "minimum": 1 },
        "hint": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: Hint for the question" },
        "explanation": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: Explanation shown after answering" },
        "media": {
          "type": "object",
          "description": "OPTIONAL: Media attachment for the question",
          "properties": {
            "type": { "enum": ["image", "video", "audio", "youtube"] },
            "url": { "type": "string", "description": "URL to media file" },
            "alt": { "type": "string", "description": "Alt text for accessibility" },
            "caption": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: Caption below media" },
            "mimeType": { "type": "string", "description": "OPTIONAL: MIME type for video/audio" },
            "videoId": { "type": "string", "description": "YouTube video ID (for youtube type)" },
            "startTime": { "type": "integer", "description": "OPTIONAL: Start time in seconds (youtube)" },
            "autoplay": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
            "loop": { "type": "boolean", "default": false },
            "muted": { "type": "boolean", "default": false }
          }
        }
      },
      "allOf": [
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "multiple-choice" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "options": {
                "type": "array",
                "minItems": 2,
                "maxItems": 6,
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "required": ["id", "isCorrect"],
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string", "description": "Text label (OPTIONAL if image provided)" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" },
                    "image": {
                      "type": "object",
                      "description": "OPTIONAL: Image for this option",
                      "properties": {
                        "url": { "type": "string" },
                        "alt": { "type": "string" }
                      }
                    }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "multiple-select" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "options": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "required": ["id", "isCorrect"],
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string", "description": "Text label (OPTIONAL if image provided)" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" },
                    "image": {
                      "type": "object",
                      "description": "OPTIONAL: Image for this option",
                      "properties": {
                        "url": { "type": "string" },
                        "alt": { "type": "string" }
                      }
                    }
                  }
                }
              },
              "partialCredit": { "type": "boolean", "default": true }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "true-false" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "correctAnswer": { "type": "boolean" }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "fill-blank" } } },
          "then": {
            "description": " CRITICAL: The 'question' field MUST contain __id__ placeholders (e.g., __b1__, __b2__) that match the blank IDs. Example: 'The liver converts ammonia into __b1__.' with blank id='b1'",
            "properties": {
              "blanks": {
                "type": "array",
                "description": "Array of blank definitions. Each blank.id must have a matching __id__ placeholder in the question text.",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string", "description": "Blank identifier (e.g., 'b1', '1', 'answer1'). Must match placeholder in question." },
                    "acceptedAnswers": { "type": "array", "items": { "type": "string" }, "description": "List of acceptable answers" },
                    "caseSensitive": { "type": "boolean", "default": false }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "matching" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "pairs": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "left": { "type": "string" },
                    "right": { "type": "string" }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "ordering" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "items": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string" },
                    "correctPosition": { "type": "integer" }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "short-answer" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "keywords": { "type": "array", "items": { "type": "string" } },
              "minKeywords": { "type": "integer" },
              "modelAnswer": { "type": "string" },
              "maxLength": { "type": "integer" }
            }
          }
        },
        {
          "if": { "properties": { "type": { "const": "image-based" } } },
          "then": {
            "properties": {
              "imageUrl": { "type": "string" },
              "imageAlt": { "type": "string" },
              "hotspots": {
                "type": "array",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "x": { "type": "number" },
                    "y": { "type": "number" },
                    "radius": { "type": "number" },
                    "label": { "type": "string" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" }
                  }
                }
              },
              "options": {
                "type": "array",
                "description": "OPTIONAL: Alternative to hotspots for multiple-choice style image questions",
                "items": {
                  "type": "object",
                  "required": ["id", "isCorrect"],
                  "properties": {
                    "id": { "type": "string" },
                    "text": { "type": "string" },
                    "isCorrect": { "type": "boolean" }
                  }
                }
              }
            }
          }
        }
      ]
    }
  }
}
```

```json
{
```

#### Example 5: Fill-Blank Question - Correct vs Incorrect Usage

** CRITICAL REQUIREMENT**: The question text MUST include `__id__` placeholders that match the blank IDs.

#####  CORRECT - Single Blank

```json
{
  "id": "q1",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The accumulation of serous fluid in the peritoneal cavity seen in cirrhosis is called __b1__.",
  "points": 10,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["ascites"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ],
  "explanation": "Ascites is the accumulation of fluid in the peritoneal cavity."
}
```

#####  CORRECT - Multiple Blanks

```json
{
  "id": "q2",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The liver converts ammonia into __b1__, which is then excreted by the __b2__.",
  "points": 15,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["urea"], "caseSensitive": false },
    { "id": "b2", "acceptedAnswers": ["kidneys", "kidney"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ],
  "explanation": "Ammonia is converted to urea by the liver and excreted by the kidneys."
}
```

#####  CORRECT - Numeric IDs

```json
{
  "id": "q3",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The heart has __1__ chambers: two __2__ and two __3__.",
  "points": 15,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "1", "acceptedAnswers": ["four", "4"], "caseSensitive": false },
    { "id": "2", "acceptedAnswers": ["atria", "atriums"], "caseSensitive": false },
    { "id": "3", "acceptedAnswers": ["ventricles"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ]
}
```

#####  INCORRECT - Missing Placeholder

```json
{
  "id": "q_wrong",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The accumulation of serous fluid in the peritoneal cavity is called _______.",
  "points": 10,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["ascites"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ]
}
```
**Problem**: Uses `_______` instead of `__b1__`. The quiz engine won't render an input field!

#####  INCORRECT - Mismatched IDs

```json
{
  "id": "q_wrong2",
  "type": "fill-blank",
  "question": "The liver converts ammonia into __answer__.",
  "points": 10,
  "blanks": [
    { "id": "b1", "acceptedAnswers": ["urea"], "caseSensitive": false }
  ]
}
```
**Problem**: Question uses `__answer__` but blank ID is `b1`. They must match exactly!

##### Key Rules for Fill-Blank Questions:
1. **Placeholder Format**: Use double underscores: `__id__` (not single `_id_` or dashes `---`)
2. **ID Matching**: Placeholder `__b1__` must match blank `"id": "b1"` exactly
3. **Multiple Blanks**: Each blank needs its own unique ID and placeholder
4. **Accepted Answers**: Provide multiple acceptable variations (e.g., `["urea", "Urea"]`)
5. **Case Sensitivity**: Set `caseSensitive: false` for most medical terminology



### Quiz Loading Methods

The quiz system supports 3 loading methods (tried in order):

| Method | Attribute | Works with file:// | Requires Server |
|--------|-----------|-------------------|-----------------|
| **JSONP (Recommended)** | `data-quiz-js` |  Yes | No |
| Fetch API | `data-quiz-src` |  No | Yes |
| Embedded JSON | `<script id="quiz-data-[id]">` |  Yes | No |

#### Method 1: JSONP Script Loading (Recommended)

**Best for:** Opening HTML files directly in browser (`file://` protocol)

Create quiz as a `.js` file that calls `window.registerQuiz()`:

```javascript
// quizzes/topic-01-quiz.js
window.registerQuiz('topic-01-quiz', {
  "schemaVersion": "1.1",
  "quizId": "topic-01-quiz",
  "metadata": { ... },
  "settings": { ... },
  "questions": [ ... ]
});
```

** CRITICAL REQUIREMENTS for Quiz Loading:**

1. **Use `window.registerQuiz()` callback**: The quiz engine expects this exact function name
   -  CORRECT: `window.registerQuiz('quiz-id', {...})`
   -  WRONG: `window.topic01QuizCallback({...})` or any other custom name

2. **Quiz ID must match**: The first parameter must match the `quizId` in the JSON
   -  CORRECT: `window.registerQuiz('topic-01-quiz', { "quizId": "topic-01-quiz", ... })`
   -  WRONG: `window.registerQuiz('topic-01', { "quizId": "topic-01-quiz", ... })`

3. **Schema Version is required**: Must include `schemaVersion: "1.1"` at the top level
   -  CORRECT: `{ "schemaVersion": "1.1", "quizId": "...", ... }`
   -  WRONG: `{ "quizId": "...", ... }` (missing schemaVersion)

4. **Metadata object is required**: Must include `metadata` with required fields
   -  CORRECT: `{ "metadata": { "title": "...", "description": "...", "difficulty": "...", "estimatedTime": 10, "passingScore": 70 } }`
   -  WRONG: `{ "title": "...", "description": "..." }` (top-level, not in metadata)

5. **Settings object is required**: Must include `settings` with configuration
   -  CORRECT: `{ "settings": { "shuffleQuestions": false, "shuffleOptions": false, "showFeedback": "always", "allowRetry": true } }`
   -  WRONG: Missing settings object entirely

6. **Use `isCorrect` in options**: Multiple-choice questions must use `isCorrect: true/false`
   -  CORRECT: `{ "id": "a", "text": "Answer", "isCorrect": true }`
   -  WRONG: `{ "id": "a", "text": "Answer" }` with separate `"correctAnswer": "a"` at question level

7. **Avoid JSON syntax errors**: Common typos that break parsing
   -  WRONG: `"text">"Answer text"` (typo: `>` instead of `:`)
   -  WRONG: Missing commas between array items or object properties
   -  WRONG: Trailing commas in JSON (not allowed in strict JSON)

**Common Quiz Loading Issues and Solutions:**

| Issue | Cause | Solution |
|-------|-------|----------|
| Quiz shows "Loading..." indefinitely | Wrong callback name or quiz ID mismatch | Use `window.registerQuiz('quiz-id', {...})` with matching IDs |
| Quiz shows error message | JSON syntax error | Check for typos like `"text">` instead of `"text":` |
| Quiz doesn't load | Missing schemaVersion or metadata | Add required top-level properties |
| Options not marked correct | Using `correctAnswer` instead of `isCorrect` | Change to `isCorrect: true/false` in each option |
| Quiz loads but questions don't display | Invalid question type or missing required fields | Verify all questions have `id`, `type`, `question`, `points` |

**Quiz File Template (Copy This):**

```javascript
// quizzes/[topic-name]-quiz.js
window.registerQuiz('[quiz-id]', {
  "schemaVersion": "1.1",
  "quizId": "[quiz-id]",
  "metadata": {
    "title": "[Quiz Title]",
    "description": "[Brief description]",
    "difficulty": "intermediate",
    "estimatedTime": 10,
    "passingScore": 70
  },
  "settings": {
    "shuffleQuestions": false,
    "shuffleOptions": false,
    "showFeedback": "always",
    "allowRetry": true
  },
  "questions": [
    {
      "id": 1,
      "type": "multiple-choice",
      "question": "[Question text]",
      "points": 1,
      "options": [
        { "id": "a", "text": "Option A", "isCorrect": false },
        { "id": "b", "text": "Option B", "isCorrect": true },
        { "id": "c", "text": "Option C", "isCorrect": false },
        { "id": "d", "text": "Option D", "isCorrect": false }
      ],
      "explanation": "[Explanation shown after answering]"
    }
  ]
});
```

HTML usage:
```html
<div class="quiz-container" 
     data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz"
     data-quiz-js="../quizzes/topic-01-quiz.js">
```

#### Method 2: Fetch API (Requires Web Server)

**Best for:** Deployment on web servers (http/https)

```html
<div class="quiz-container" 
     data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz"
     data-quiz-src="../quizzes/topic-01-quiz.json">
```

#### Method 3: Embedded JSON

**Best for:** Single-file distribution

```html
<script type="application/json" id="quiz-data-topic-01-quiz">
{
  "schemaVersion": "1.0",
  "quizId": "topic-01-quiz",
  ...
}
</script>

<div class="quiz-container" data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz">
```

### Quiz HTML Integration

Add quiz sections to topic pages using this structure:

```html
<!-- Quiz Section -->
<section class="quiz-section" id="topic-quiz" aria-labelledby="quiz-title">
    <div class="quiz-header">
        <div class="quiz-badge">
            <span class="quiz-icon"></span>
            <span>Knowledge Check</span>
        </div>
        <h2 id="quiz-title" class="quiz-title">Test Your Understanding</h2>
        <p class="quiz-description">Complete this quiz to assess your comprehension of the topic.</p>
    </div>
    
    <!-- Quiz Container - JSONP method (works with file://) -->
    <div class="quiz-container" 
         data-quiz-id="topic-01-quiz"
         data-quiz-js="../quizzes/topic-01-quiz.js">
        
        <!-- Loading State -->
        <div class="quiz-loading">
            <div class="quiz-spinner"></div>
            <p>Loading quiz...</p>
        </div>
        
        <!-- Quiz Content (injected by JS) -->
        <div class="quiz-content" hidden></div>
        
        <!-- Quiz Results (shown after completion) -->
        <div class="quiz-results" hidden></div>
    </div>
</section>
```

### Updated Directory Structure (v9.4)

```
project-name/
 index.html                           # Table of Contents (Rich UI)
 quiz-hub.html                        # NEW: Central quiz listing page
 topics/
    topic-01-introduction.html       # Topic pages with quiz sections
    topic-02-concepts.html
    ...
 quizzes/                             # Quiz JSON files
    topic-01-quiz.json               # Quiz for topic 01
    topic-02-quiz.json               # Quiz for topic 02
    ...
 assets/
    images/
        [ID]g-[PageNum]-[SeqNum].ext # All extracted images
 styles/
    main.css                         # Main stylesheet (v9.4 with quiz styles)
 js/
     navigation.js                    # Navigation helpers
     theme.js                         # Dark mode toggle
     interactions.js                  # UI interactions
     quiz.js                          # Quiz engine
     quiz-hub.js                      # NEW: Quiz hub manager
```

### Quiz Access Points (v9.4)

Users can access quizzes through multiple entry points:

1. **Floating Quiz Button** - Fixed button on topic pages that jumps to the quiz section
2. **Header Meta Link** - "Quiz Available" link in topic header
3. **Navigation Bar** - "All Quizzes" button in top/bottom navigation
4. **Quiz Hub Page** - Central page listing all quizzes with:
   - Progress tracking (completed, in-progress, not started)
   - Difficulty filtering
   - Best scores display
   - Links to both quiz and topic review
5. **Index Page** - Quiz indicators on topic cards (optional)

### Template Files

| Template | Purpose |
|----------|---------|
| `topic-template-v1.2.html` | Topic page with quiz section and floating button |
| `quiz-hub-template.html` | Quiz hub page listing all quizzes |
| `exam-template.html` | Comprehensive exam page with topic breakdown |
| `index-template-v1.1.html` | Index page (add quiz indicators to topic cards) |

### Quiz Implementation Checklist

For each topic with a quiz:

1.  **Create Quiz JSON**: Create `quizzes/topic-XX-quiz.json` following the schema
2.  **Schema Version**: Include `"schemaVersion": "1.0"` for compatibility
3.  **Metadata Complete**: Fill in title, topicId, difficulty, estimatedTime, passingScore
4.  **Question Variety**: Use appropriate question types for the content
5.  **Points Allocation**: Assign points based on question difficulty
6.  **Explanations**: Provide explanations for all questions
7.  **Hints (Optional)**: Add hints for challenging questions
8.  **Media (Optional)**: Add images/videos to questions if helpful
9.  **HTML Integration**: Use `topic-template-v1.2.html` with quiz section
10.  **Quiz Hub**: Add quiz card to `quiz-hub.html`
11.  **Script Loading**: Include quiz.js and quiz-hub.js
12.  **Accessibility**: Verify keyboard navigation and screen reader support
13.  **Dark Mode**: Test quiz appearance in both themes
14.  **Mobile Testing**: Verify responsive behavior on small screens

### Quiz Best Practices


#### Question Writing Guidelines
- **Clear Language**: Use unambiguous wording
- **Single Concept**: Test one concept per question
- **Plausible Distractors**: Make incorrect options believable
- **Avoid Negatives**: Minimize "NOT" or "EXCEPT" questions
- **Consistent Length**: Keep option lengths similar

#### Difficulty Balancing
- **Beginner**: 60% recall, 30% comprehension, 10% application
- **Intermediate**: 40% recall, 40% comprehension, 20% application
- **Advanced**: 20% recall, 40% comprehension, 40% application/analysis

#### Points Distribution
- **Easy Questions**: 5-10 points
- **Medium Questions**: 10-15 points
- **Hard Questions**: 15-25 points
- **Complex (Matching/Ordering)**: 20-30 points

---

## Comprehensive Exam System

### Overview

In addition to per-topic quizzes, the system supports comprehensive exams that test knowledge across all course topics. These exams provide:

- **Cross-topic assessment**: Questions from multiple topics in a single exam
- **Topic-based scoring**: See performance breakdown by topic
- **Exam types**: Support for comprehensive, midterm, final, and practice exams
- **Progress tracking**: Track exam attempts and best scores

### Exam Types

| Type | Description | Use Case |
|------|-------------|----------|
| `comprehensive` | All topics, full coverage | Final assessment |
| `midterm` | First half of topics | Mid-course check |
| `final` | Second half or cumulative | End of course |
| `practice` | Random selection | Self-study |

### Comprehensive Exam JSON Schema

Comprehensive exams use the same quiz schema with additional fields:

```javascript
// quizzes/comprehensive-exam.js
registerQuiz("comprehensive-exam", {
  "schemaVersion": "1.0",
  "quizId": "comprehensive-exam",
  "metadata": {
    "title": "Comprehensive Final Exam",
    "description": "Test your knowledge across all course topics",
    "examType": "comprehensive",           // NEW: Exam type
    "topicsCovered": ["topic-01", "topic-02", "topic-03"],  // NEW: Topics included
    "difficulty": "advanced",
    "estimatedTime": 45,
    "passingScore": 75,
    "createdAt": "2025-12-25T00:00:00Z",
    "tags": ["final", "comprehensive", "all-topics"]
  },
  "settings": {
    "shuffleQuestions": true,
    "shuffleOptions": true,
    "showFeedback": "end",
    "allowRetry": true,
    "showCorrectAnswers": true,
    "timeLimit": 2700                      // 45 minutes in seconds
  },
  "questions": [
    {
      "id": "comp-q1",
      "type": "multiple-choice",
      "question": "From Topic 1: What is the capital of France?",
      "points": 10,
      "topicId": "topic-01",               // NEW: Topic identifier
      "topicName": "Geography Basics",     // NEW: Topic display name
      "options": [
        { "id": "a", "text": "London", "isCorrect": false },
        { "id": "b", "text": "Paris", "isCorrect": true },
        { "id": "c", "text": "Berlin", "isCorrect": false }
      ],
      "explanation": "Paris is the capital of France."
    }
    // More questions from different topics...
  ]
});
```

### Key Differences from Regular Quizzes

| Feature | Regular Quiz | Comprehensive Exam |
|---------|--------------|-------------------|
| Scope | Single topic | Multiple topics |
| `topicId` per question | Not needed | Required |
| `topicName` per question | Not needed | Required |
| `examType` in metadata | Not used | Required |
| `topicsCovered` in metadata | Not used | Required |
| Results display | Overall score | Score + topic breakdown |

### Exam Template

Use `exam-template.html` for comprehensive exams:

```html
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en" data-theme="light">
<head>
    <title>[EXAM TITLE] - [COURSE NAME]</title>
    <link rel="stylesheet" href="styles/main.css">
</head>
<body>
    <!-- Exam Header with Info Cards -->
    <header class="document-header exam-header">
        <div class="header-badge exam-badge">
            <span></span>
            <span>Comprehensive Exam</span>
        </div>
        <h1 class="document-title">[EXAM TITLE]</h1>
        
        <!-- Exam Info Cards -->
        <div class="exam-info-cards">
            <div class="exam-info-card">
                <span class="info-icon"></span>
                <span class="info-value">[X] Topics</span>
                <span class="info-label">Covered</span>
            </div>
            <div class="exam-info-card">
                <span class="info-icon"></span>
                <span class="info-value">[X] Questions</span>
                <span class="info-label">Total</span>
            </div>
            <!-- More info cards... -->
        </div>

        <!-- Topics Covered List -->
        <div class="exam-topics-covered">
            <h3>Topics Covered:</h3>
            <div class="topics-list">
                <span class="topic-tag">Topic 1: [Name]</span>
                <span class="topic-tag">Topic 2: [Name]</span>
            </div>
        </div>
    </header>

    <!-- Exam Quiz Section -->
    <section class="quiz-section exam-section" id="exam-quiz">
        <div class="quiz-container" 
             data-quiz-id="comprehensive-exam"
             data-quiz-js="quizzes/comprehensive-exam.js">
            <div class="quiz-loading">...</div>
            <div class="quiz-content" hidden></div>
            <div class="quiz-results" hidden></div>
        </div>
    </section>

    <script src="js/theme.js"></script>
    <script src="js/quiz.js"></script>
</body>
</html>
```

### Topic-Based Results Display

When a comprehensive exam is submitted, the results show:

1. **Overall Score**: Total percentage and pass/fail status
2. **Questions Correct**: X out of Y questions
3. **Points Earned**: X out of Y points
4. **Time Taken**: Minutes and seconds
5. **Topic Breakdown**: Performance by topic with:
   - Topic name
   - Percentage score
   - Progress bar (color-coded: green 70%, yellow 50%, red <50%)
   - Questions correct and points earned per topic

```html
        </div>

            <span> [X] Questions</span>
            <span> [X] Minutes</span>
        </div>
    </div>

        Take Final Exam 
    </a>
</div>
```

### Comprehensive Exam Checklist

1.  **Create Exam File**: Create `quizzes/comprehensive-exam.js`
2.  **Include All Topics**: Add `topicsCovered` array in metadata
3.  **Tag Questions**: Add `topicId` and `topicName` to each question
4.  **Balance Topics**: Include proportional questions from each topic
5.  **Set Exam Type**: Add `examType: "comprehensive"` to metadata
6.  **Create Exam Page**: Use `exam-template.html`
7.  **Update Quiz Hub**: Add exam banner to quiz-hub.html
8.  **Test Topic Scoring**: Verify topic breakdown displays correctly
9.  **Test All Question Types**: Ensure all question types work in exam context
